<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a></div>
<p>Murray Bookchin (January 14, 1921 – July 30, 2006)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[55]</a></sup> was an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_socialism" title="Libertarian socialism">libertarian socialist</a> author, orator, and philosopher. In 1958, Murray Bookchin defined himself as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube2007_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-youtube2007-60">[56]</a></sup> seeing parallels between anarchism and ecology. His first book, <i><a href="/wiki/Our_Synthetic_Environment" title="Our Synthetic Environment">Our Synthetic Environment</a>,</i> was published under the <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonym</a> Lewis Herber in 1962, a few months before <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Carson" title="Rachel Carson">Rachel Carson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Spring" title="Silent Spring">Silent Spring</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup> The book described a broad range of environmental ills but received little attention because of its political radicalism. His groundbreaking essay "Ecology and Revolutionary Thought" introduced <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a> as a concept in radical politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup> In 1968 he founded another group that published the influential <i>Anarchos</i> magazine, which published that and other innovative essays on post-scarcity and on ecological technologies such as solar and wind energy, and on decentralization and miniaturization. Lecturing throughout the United States, he helped popularize the concept of ecology to the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture" title="Counterculture">counterculture</a>.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Post-Scarcity_Anarchism" title="Post-Scarcity Anarchism">Post-Scarcity Anarchism</a></i> is a collection of <a href="/wiki/Essay" title="Essay">essays</a> written by <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a> and first published in 1971 by Ramparts Press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[59]</a></sup> It outlines the possible form <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a> might take under conditions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post_scarcity" title="Post scarcity">post-scarcity</a>. It is one of Bookchin's major works,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup> and its radical thesis provoked controversy for being <a href="/wiki/Utopia" title="Utopia">utopian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Messianism" title="Messianism">messianic</a> in its faith in the liberatory potential of <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-call_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-call-65">[61]</a></sup> Bookchin argues that <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial societies</a> are also post-scarcity societies, and can thus imagine "the fulfillment of the social and cultural potentialities latent in a technology of abundance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-call_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-call-65">[61]</a></sup> The self-administration of society is now made possible by technological advancement and, when technology is used in an ecologically sensitive manner, the revolutionary potential of society will be much changed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AK_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-AK-66">[62]</a></sup> In 1982, his book <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Ecology_of_Freedom:_The_Emergence_and_Dissolution_of_Hierarchy" title="The Ecology of Freedom: The Emergence and Dissolution of Hierarchy">The Ecology of Freedom</a></i> had a profound impact on the emerging ecology movement, both in the United States and abroad. He was a principal figure in the Burlington Greens in 1986-90, an ecology group that ran candidates for city council on a program to create neighborhood democracy. In <i>From Urbanization to Cities</i> (originally published in 1987 as <i>The Rise of Urbanization and the Decline of Citizenship</i>), Bookchin traced the democratic traditions that influenced his political philosophy and defined the implementation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian_municipalism" title="Libertarian municipalism">libertarian municipalism</a> concept. A few years later <i>The Politics of Social Ecology</i>, written by his partner of 20 years, <a href="/wiki/Janet_Biehl" title="Janet Biehl">Janet Biehl</a>, briefly summarized these ideas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacques_Ellul">Jacques Ellul</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Jacques Ellul">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Ellul" title="Jacques Ellul">Jacques Ellul</a></div>
<p>Jacques Ellul (January 6, 1912 – May 19, 1994) was a French <a href="/wiki/Philosopher" title="Philosopher">philosopher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurisprudence" title="Jurisprudence">law professor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociologist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lay_theologian" title="Lay theologian">lay theologian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christian_anarchism" title="Christian anarchism">Christian anarchist</a>. He wrote several books about Christianity, the technological society, propaganda, and the interaction between <a href="/wiki/Political_science_of_religion" title="Political science of religion">religion and politics</a>. Professor of History and the Sociology of Institutions on the Faculty of Law and Economic Sciences at the University of Bordeaux, he authored 58 books and more than a thousand articles over his lifetime in all, the dominant theme of which has been the threat to human freedom and religion created by modern technique. The Ellulian concept of technique is briefly defined within the "Notes to Reader" section of <i>The Technological Society</i> (1964). What many consider to be Ellul's most important work, <i>The Technological Society</i> (1964) was originally titled: <i>La Technique: L'enjeu du siècle</i> (literally, "The Stake of the Century").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup> In it, Ellul set forth seven characteristics of modern technology that make efficiency a necessity: <a href="/wiki/Rationalization_(sociology)" title="Rationalization (sociology)">rationality</a>, artificiality, automatism of technical choice, self-augmentation, <a href="/wiki/Monism" title="Monism">monism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universalism" title="Universalism">universalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TechnologicalSociety_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-TechnologicalSociety-68">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>For Ellul the rationality of technique enforces logical and mechanical organization through division of labor, the setting of production standards, etc. And it creates an artificial system which "eliminates or subordinates the natural world." Today, he argues, the technological society is generally held sacred (cf. Saint Steve Jobs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup>). Since he defines technique as "the totality of methods rationally arrived at, and having absolute efficiency (for a given stage of development) in every field of human activity",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup> it is clear that his sociological analysis focuses not on the society of machines as such, but on the society of "efficient techniques".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_developments">Contemporary developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Contemporary developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Notable contemporary writers espousing green anarchism include <a href="/wiki/Layla_AbdelRahim" title="Layla AbdelRahim">Layla AbdelRahim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derrick_Jensen" title="Derrick Jensen">Derrick Jensen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Semprun" title="Jaime Semprun">Jaime Semprun</a>, George Draffan, <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starhawk" title="Starhawk">Starhawk</a> and  <a href="/wiki/Alan_Carter_(philosopher)" title="Alan Carter (philosopher)">Alan Carter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_ecology_and_Communalism">Social ecology and Communalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Social ecology and Communalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_ecology_(theory)" title="Social ecology (theory)">Social ecology (theory)</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communalism_(Political_Philosophy)" title="Communalism (Political Philosophy)">Communalism (Political Philosophy)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Murray_Bookchin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4286" data-file-width="3429" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Murray_Bookchin.jpg/180px-Murray_Bookchin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Murray_Bookchin.jpg/270px-Murray_Bookchin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Murray_Bookchin.jpg/360px-Murray_Bookchin.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Murray_Bookchin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a></div></div></div><p>Social ecology is closely related to the work and ideas of <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a> and influenced by anarchist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a>. Social ecologists assert that the present <a href="/wiki/Ecological_crisis" title="Ecological crisis">ecological crisis</a> has its roots in human social problems, and that the domination of human-over-nature stems from the domination of human-over-human.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bookchin later developed a political philosophy to complement social ecology which he called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communalism_(Political_Philosophy)" title="Communalism (Political Philosophy)">Communalism</a>" (spelled with a capital "C" to differentiate it from other forms of communalism). While originally conceived as a form of <a href="/wiki/Social_anarchism" title="Social anarchism">Social anarchism</a>, he later developed Communalism into a separate ideology which incorporates what he saw as the most beneficial elements of Anarchism, Marxism, syndicalism, and radical ecology.
</p><p>Politically, Communalists advocate a network of directly democratic citizens' assemblies in individual communities/cities organized in a confederal fashion. This method used to achieve this is called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian_Municipalism" title="Libertarian Municipalism">Libertarian Municipalism</a> which involves the establishment of face-to-face democratic institutions which are to grow and expand confederally with the goal of eventually replacing the nation-state.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Janet_Biehl" title="Janet Biehl">Janet Biehl</a> (born 1953) is a writer associated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_ecology_(theory)" title="Social ecology (theory)">social ecology</a>, the body of ideas developed and publicized by <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a>. In 1986, she attended the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_for_Social_Ecology" title="Institute for Social Ecology">Institute for Social Ecology</a> and there, began a collaborative relationship with Bookchin, working intensively with him over the next two decades in the explication of social ecology from their shared home in <a href="/wiki/Burlington,_Vermont" title="Burlington, Vermont">Burlington, Vermont</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1987 to 2000, she and Bookchin co-wrote and co-published the theoretical newsletter <i>Green Perspectives</i>, later renamed <i>Left Green Perspectives</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup> She is the editor and compiler of <i>The Murray Bookchin Reader</i> (1997);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup> the author of <i>The Politics of Social Ecology: Libertarian Municipalism</i> (1998) and <i>Rethinking Ecofeminist Politics</i> (1991); and coauthor (with Peter Staudenmaier) of <i>Ecofascism: Lessons from the German Experience</i> (1995).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_Anarchist"><i>Green Anarchist</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Green Anarchist">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Green_Anarchist" title="Green Anarchist">Green Anarchist</a></div>
<p>The magazine <i>Green Anarchist</i> was for a while the principal voice in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> advocating green anarchism, an explicit fusion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian_socialist" title="Libertarian socialist">libertarian socialist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological" title="Ecological">ecological</a> thinking. Founded after the 1984 <a href="/wiki/Stop_the_City" title="Stop the City">Stop the City</a> protests, the magazine was launched in the summer of that year by an editorial collective consisting of <a href="/wiki/Alan_Albon" title="Alan Albon">Alan Albon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hunt_(editor)" title="Richard Hunt (editor)">Richard Hunt</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marcus_Christo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marcus Christo (page does not exist)">Marcus Christo</a>. Early issues featured a range of broadly anarchist and ecological ideas, bringing together groups and individuals as varied as <a href="/wiki/Class_War" title="Class War">Class War</a>, veteran anarchist writer <a href="/wiki/Colin_Ward" title="Colin Ward">Colin Ward</a>, anarcho-punk band <a href="/wiki/Crass" title="Crass">Crass</a>, as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_Convoy" title="Peace Convoy">Peace Convoy</a>, anti-nuclear campaigners, <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> activists and so on. However, the diversity that many saw as the publication's greatest strength quickly led to irreconcilable arguments between the essentially <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">pacifist</a> approach of Albon and Christo, and the advocacy of violent confrontation with the State favoured by Hunt. During the 1990s <i>Green Anarchist</i> came under the helm of an editorial collective that included <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Rogers_(Green_Anarchist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Paul Rogers (Green Anarchist) (page does not exist)">Paul Rogers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Booth" title="Steve Booth">Steve Booth</a> and others, during which period the publication became increasingly aligned with <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">primitivism</a>, an anti-civilization philosophy advocated by writers such as <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fredy_Perlman" title="Fredy Perlman">Fredy Perlman</a>. Starting in 1995, <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a> Police began a series of at least 56 raids, <a href="/wiki/Code_name" title="Code name">code named</a> 'Operation Washington', that eventually resulted in the August to November 1997 <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> trial of Green Anarchist editors Booth, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Saxon_Wood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Saxon Wood (page does not exist)">Saxon Wood</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Noel_Molland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Noel Molland (page does not exist)">Noel Molland</a> and Paul Rogers, as well as <a href="/wiki/Animal_Liberation_Front" title="Animal Liberation Front">Animal Liberation Front</a> (ALF) Press Officer <a href="/wiki/Robin_Webb" title="Robin Webb">Robin Webb</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_Liberation_Front_Supporters_Group" title="Animal Liberation Front Supporters Group">Animal Liberation Front Supporters Group</a> (ALFSG) newsletter editor Simon Russell. The defendants organised the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GANDALF_Defence_campaign" title="GANDALF Defence campaign">GANDALF Defence campaign</a>. Three of the editors of Green Anarchist, Noel Molland, Saxon Wood and Booth were jailed for 'conspiracy to incite'. However, all three were shortly afterwards released on appeal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fredy_Perlman">Fredy Perlman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fredy Perlman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fredy_Perlman" title="Fredy Perlman">Fredy Perlman</a></div>
<p>Fredy Perlman (August 20, 1934 – July 26, 1985) was a Czech-born, naturalised American author, publisher and militant. His most popular work, the book <i><a href="/wiki/Against_His-Story,_Against_Leviathan" title="Against His-Story, Against Leviathan">Against His-Story, Against Leviathan</a>!</i>, details the rise of state domination with a retelling of history through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hobbesian" title="Hobbesian">Hobbesian</a> metaphor of the <a href="/wiki/Leviathan_(Hobbes_book)" title="Leviathan (Hobbes book)">Leviathan</a>. The book remains a major source of inspiration for anti-civilization perspectives in <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_anarchism" title="Contemporary anarchism">contemporary anarchism</a>, most notably on the thought of philosopher <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anarcho-primitivism">Anarcho-primitivism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Anarcho-primitivism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">Anarcho-primitivism</a></div>
<p>Anarcho-primitivism is an <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a> critique of the origins and progress of <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>. According to anarcho-primitivism, the shift from <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> to <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> subsistence gave rise to <a href="/wiki/Social_stratification" title="Social stratification">social stratification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_alienation" title="Social alienation">alienation</a>. Anarcho-primitivists advocate a return to non-"civilized" ways of life through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deindustrialisation" title="Deindustrialisation">deindustrialisation</a>, abolition of the <a href="/wiki/Division_of_labour" title="Division of labour">division of labour</a> or <a href="/wiki/Specialization_(functional)" title="Specialization (functional)">specialization</a>, and abandonment of large-scale organization <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technologies</a>. There are other non-anarchist forms of primitivism, and not all primitivists point to the same phenomenon as the source of modern, civilized problems. Anarcho-primitivists are often distinguished by their focus on the <a href="/wiki/Praxis_(process)" title="Praxis (process)">praxis</a> of achieving a <a href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> state of being through "<a href="/wiki/Rewilding_(anarchism)" title="Rewilding (anarchism)">rewilding</a>".
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Zerzan">John Zerzan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: John Zerzan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="512" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG/180px-John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG/270px-John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG/360px-John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Zerzan_SF_-_Anarchist_Bookfair_%2706.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a>, anarcho-primitivism theorist</div></div></div>
<p>John Zerzan is an American <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">primitivist</a> philosopher and author. His works criticize agricultural <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a> as inherently oppressive, and advocate drawing upon the ways of life of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter_gatherer" title="Hunter gatherer">hunter gatherers</a> as an inspiration for what a free society should look like. Some subjects of his criticism include <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism#Critique_of_symbolic_culture" title="Anarcho-primitivism">symbolic thought</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> and art) and the concept of time.
</p><p>His five major books are <i>Elements of Refusal</i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Future_Primitive_and_Other_Essays" title="Future Primitive and Other Essays">Future Primitive and Other Essays</a></i> (1994), <i>Running on Emptiness</i> (2002), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Against_Civilization:_Readings_and_Reflections" title="Against Civilization: Readings and Reflections">Against Civilization: Readings and Reflections</a></i> (2005) and <i>Twilight of the Machines</i> (2008). Zerzan was one of the editors of <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Anarchy" title="Green Anarchy">Green Anarchy</a></i>, a controversial journal of anarcho-primitivist and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurrectionary_anarchist" title="Insurrectionary anarchist">insurrectionary anarchist</a> thought. He is also the host of <i>Anarchy Radio</i> in Eugene on the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon" title="University of Oregon">University of Oregon</a>'s radio station <a href="/wiki/KWVA" title="KWVA">KWVA</a>. He has also served as a contributing editor at <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchy_Magazine" title="Anarchy Magazine">Anarchy Magazine</a></i> and has been published in magazines such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AdBusters" title="AdBusters">AdBusters</a></i>. He does extensive speaking tours around the world, and is married to an independent consultant to museums and other nonprofit organizations. In 1974, Black and Red Press published <i>Unions Against Revolution</i> by Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultra-left" title="Ultra-left">ultra-left</a> theorist <a href="/wiki/Grandizo_Munis" title="Grandizo Munis">Grandizo Munis</a> that included an essay by Zerzan which previously appeared in the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Telos_(journal)" title="Telos (journal)">Telos</a></i>. Over the next 20 years, Zerzan became intimately involved with the <i><a href="/wiki/Fifth_Estate_(periodical)" title="Fifth Estate (periodical)">Fifth Estate</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchy:_A_Journal_of_Desire_Armed" title="Anarchy: A Journal of Desire Armed">Anarchy: A Journal of Desire Armed</a></i>, <i>Demolition Derby </i> and other anarchist periodicals. He began to question civilization in the early 80's, after having sought to confront issues around the neutrality of technology and division of labour, at the time when <a href="/wiki/Fredy_Perlman" title="Fredy Perlman">Fredy Perlman</a> was making similar conclusions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_Anarchy"><i>Green Anarchy</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Green Anarchy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Green_Anarchy" title="Green Anarchy">Green Anarchy</a></div>
<p><i>Green Anarchy</i> was a <a href="/wiki/Magazine" title="Magazine">magazine</a> published by a collective located in <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene, Oregon</a>. The magazine's focus was <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">primitivism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-left_anarchy" title="Post-left anarchy">post-left anarchy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radical_environmentalism" title="Radical environmentalism">radical environmentalism</a>, African American struggles, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a> resistance, indigenous resistance, earth and animal liberation, <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalism</a> and supporting <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoners</a>. It had a circulation of 8,000, partly in prisons, the prison subscribers given free copies of each issue as stated in the magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup> Green Anarchy was started in 2000 and in 2009 the Green Anarchy website shut down, leaving a final, brief message about the cessation of the magazine's publication. The subtitle of the magazine is "An Anti-Civilization Journal of Theory and Action". Author <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a> was one of the publication's editors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Species_Traitor"><i>Species Traitor</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Species Traitor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Species_Traitor" title="Species Traitor">Species Traitor</a></div>
<p><i>Species Traitor</i> is a sporadically published journal of <a href="/wiki/Insurrectionary_anarchism" title="Insurrectionary anarchism">insurrectionary</a> <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">anarcho-primitivism</a>. It is printed as a project of Black and Green Network and edited by anarcho-primitivist writer, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Tucker_(anarchist)" title="Kevin Tucker (anarchist)">Kevin Tucker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pittsburghcitypapertucker_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-pittsburghcitypapertucker-80">[76]</a></sup> ST was initially labeled as a project of the Coalition Against Civilization (CAC) and the Black and Green Network (BAG). The CAC was started towards the end of 1999 in the aftermath of the massive street protests in Eugene (Reclaim the Streets) and in Seattle (WTO) of that year. That aftermath gave a new voice and standing for green anarchist and <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">anarcho-primitivist</a> writers and viewpoints within both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a> milieu and the culture at large. The first issue came out in winter of 2000-2001 (currently out of print) and contained a mix of reprints and some original articles from <a href="/wiki/Derrick_Jensen" title="Derrick Jensen">Derrick Jensen</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a> among others. Issue two came in the following year in the wake of Sept. 11 and took a major step from the first issue in becoming something of its own rather than another mouthpiece of green anarchist rhetoric. The articles took a more in depth direction opening a more <a href="/wiki/Analytic_induction" title="Analytic induction">analytical</a> and critical draw between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchy_(word)" title="Anarchy (word)">anarchy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a>, attacks on <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">Reason</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myth_of_Progress" title="Myth of Progress">Progress/linear</a> views of human history and Future that stand at the base of the ideology of <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vegananarchism">Vegananarchism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Vegananarchism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veganarchism" title="Veganarchism">Veganarchism</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veganarchism" title="Veganarchism">Veganarchism</a> or vegan anarchism, is the <a href="/wiki/Political_philosophy" title="Political philosophy">political philosophy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Veganism" title="Veganism">veganism</a> (more specifically <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_liberation_movement" title="Animal liberation movement">animal liberation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earth_liberation" title="Earth liberation">earth liberation</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alfsgjonny_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-alfsgjonny-81">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-veganarchy_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-veganarchy-82">[78]</a></sup> creating a combined <a href="/wiki/Praxis_(process)" title="Praxis (process)">praxis</a> that is designed to be a means for <a href="/wiki/Social_revolution" title="Social revolution">social revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>6</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup> This encompasses viewing the <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> as unnecessary and harmful to animals, both <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human</a> and <a href="/wiki/Non-human" title="Non-human">non-human</a>, whilst practising a vegan lifestyle. It is either perceived as a combined theory, or that both philosophies are essentially the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>inside page</span></sup> It is further described as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-speciesist" title="Anti-speciesist">anti-speciesist</a> perspective on green anarchism, or an anarchist perspective on animal liberation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-3"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup>
</p><p>Veganarchists typically view oppressive dynamics within society to be interconnected, from <a href="/wiki/Statism" title="Statism">statism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexism</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_supremacy" title="Human supremacy">human supremacy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-4"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>7</span></sup> and redefine veganism as a <a href="/wiki/Political_radicalism" title="Political radicalism">radical</a> philosophy that sees the state as harmful to animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-5"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>9</span></sup> Those who believe in veganarchy can be either against reform for animals or for it, although do not limit goals to changes within the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-6"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick1997_83-7"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick1997-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>12</span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Layla_AbdelRahim">Layla AbdelRahim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Layla AbdelRahim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Layla_AbdelRahim" title="Layla AbdelRahim">Layla AbdelRahim</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Layla_AbdelRahim" title="Layla AbdelRahim">Layla AbdelRahim</a> is a Canadian <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropologist</a> and author. Her work critiques <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technologies</a>, and, what she calls a "predatory anthropology".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[80]</a></sup> In <i>Children's Literature, Domestication, and Social Foundation: Narratives of Civilization and Wilderness</i> (2015), she attributes the <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> to the human choice of hunting as a cultural choice for subsistence. This anthropological revolution in human self-construction as <a href="/wiki/Predation" title="Predation">predator</a>, she argues, generated the need for developing the technologies that would ensure the propagation of a predatory culture and violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbdelRahim_2015_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-AbdelRahim_2015-85">[81]</a></sup> "The first of these technologies is... the technology of absence. ...This entails physical and emotional absence, but also includes a metaphysical dimension, since technological development is literally linked to death. Namely, the rise of hunting, i.e. killing of others for food, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Palaeolithic" title="Upper Palaeolithic">Upper Palaeolithic</a> period in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> led some human groups to develop hunting technologies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbdelRahim_2015_15_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-AbdelRahim_2015_15-86">[82]</a></sup> She cites palaeoanthropologist <a href="/wiki/Clive_Gamble" title="Clive Gamble">Clive Gamble</a> who connects this development in <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a> technologies to <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup> and the work of <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Borshay_Lee" title="Richard Borshay Lee">Richard Lee</a> (1988) who links the appearance of human language to the rise in hunting activities during that period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup> AbdelRahim concludes that <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a> "thus led to <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a>, and both of these cultures of subsistence kill intentionally and on a systematic basis".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbdelRahim_2015_15_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-AbdelRahim_2015_15-86">[82]</a></sup> Civilization with its cultural, political, and social institutions that classify living beings for the purpose of exploitation, she says, is the material manifestation of this cultural choice and anthropology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbdelRahim_2015_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-AbdelRahim_2015-85">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Wild Children – Domesticated Dreams: Civilization and the Birth of Education</i> (2013) argues that civilized child rearing cultures are based on the principles of animal domestication. The institutions of education are responsible for the generation of the epistemology of predation and for the propagation of its ideology through scientific texts, pedagogical methods, and fictional narratives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_liberation">Total liberation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Total liberation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Total_liberation" title="Total liberation">Total liberation</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Total_liberation" title="Total liberation">Total liberationism</a> is a form of green anarchism that combines an opposition to all forms of human oppression with a commitment to animal and earth liberation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup> Whilst more conventional approaches to anarchist politics typically maintain a <a href="/wiki/Tacit_assumption" title="Tacit assumption">tacit assumption</a> of anthropocentrism, proponents of total liberation espouse a holistic revolutionary strategy aimed at identifying the intersections between all forms of domination and social hierarchy, and building alliances between individual political movements in order to integrate them into a single movement aimed at abolishing a range of social structures such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_state" title="The state">the state</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heterosexism" title="Heterosexism">heterosexism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cissexism" title="Cissexism">cissexism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disablism" title="Disablism">disablism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">ageism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speciesism" title="Speciesism">speciesism</a>, and ecological domination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[87]</a></sup> As David Pellow summarises: </p><blockquote><p>The concept of total liberation stems from a determination to understand and combat all forms of inequality and oppression. I propose that it comprises four pillars: (1) an ethic of justice and anti-oppression inclusive of humans, nonhuman animals, and ecosystems; (2) anarchism; (3) anti-capitalism; and (4) an embrace of direct action tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[88]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Derrick_Jensen">Derrick Jensen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Derrick Jensen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Derrick_Jensen" title="Derrick Jensen">Derrick Jensen</a></div>
<p>Derrick Jensen is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People_of_the_United_States" title="People of the United States">American</a> author and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_activist" title="Environmental activist">environmental activist</a> (and critic of mainstream environmentalism) living in <a href="/wiki/Crescent_City,_California" title="Crescent City, California">Crescent City</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[89]</a></sup> Jensen's work is sometimes characterized as <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">anarcho-primitivist</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup> although he has categorically rejected that label, describing primitivist as a "racist way to describe indigenous peoples." He prefers to be called "<a href="/wiki/Indigenism" title="Indigenism">indigenist</a>" or an "ally to the indigenous," because "indigenous peoples have had the only sustainable human social organizations, and... we need to recognize that we [colonizers] are all living on stolen land."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>A Language Older Than Words</i> uses the lens of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> to look at the larger violence of <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">western culture</a>. <i>The Culture of Make Believe</i> begins by exploring <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Misogyny" title="Misogyny">misogyny</a> and moves to examine how this culture's economic system leads inevitably to hatred and atrocity. <i>Strangely Like War</i> is about <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>. <i>Walking on Water</i> is about <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> (It begins: "As is true for most people I know, I've always loved learning. As is also true for most people I know, I always hated school. Why is that?").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[93]</a></sup> <i>Welcome to the Machine</i> is about <a href="/wiki/Surveillance" title="Surveillance">surveillance</a>, and more broadly about science and what he perceives to be a Western obsession with control. <i>Resistance Against Empire</i> consists of interviews with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=J._W._Smith&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="J. W. Smith (page does not exist)">J. W. Smith</a> (on poverty), <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Bales" title="Kevin Bales">Kevin Bales</a> (on slavery), Anuradha Mittal (on hunger), <a href="/wiki/Juliet_Schor" title="Juliet Schor">Juliet Schor</a> ('globalization' and environmental degradation), <a href="/wiki/Ramsey_Clark" title="Ramsey Clark">Ramsey Clark</a> (on US 'defense'), Stephen Schwartz (editor of <i>The Nonproliferation Review</i>, on nukes), <a href="/wiki/Alfred_W._McCoy" title="Alfred W. McCoy">Alfred McCoy</a> (politics and heroin), <a href="/wiki/Christian_Parenti" title="Christian Parenti">Christian Parenti</a> (the US prison system), <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Albrecht" title="Katherine Albrecht">Katherine Albrecht</a> (on RFID), and <a href="/wiki/Robert_W._McChesney" title="Robert W. McChesney">Robert McChesney</a> (on (freedom of) the media) conducted between 1999 and 2004. <i>Endgame</i> is about what he describes as the inherent <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/unsustainability" title="wikt:unsustainability">unsustainability</a> of civilization. In this book he asks: "Do you believe that this culture will undergo a voluntary transformation to a sane and sustainable way of living?" Nearly everyone he talks to says no. His next question is: "How would this understanding — that this culture will not voluntarily stop destroying the natural world, eliminating indigenous cultures, exploiting the poor, and killing those who resist — shift our strategy and tactics? The answer? Nobody knows, because we never talk about it: we're too busy pretending the culture will undergo a magical transformation." <i>Endgame</i>, he says, is "about that shift in strategy, and in tactics."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup> Jensen co-wrote the book <i>Deep Green Resistance: Strategy to Save the Planet</i> with <a href="/wiki/Lierre_Keith" title="Lierre Keith">Lierre Keith</a> and Aric McBay
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CrimethInc.">CrimethInc.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: CrimethInc.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/CrimethInc." title="CrimethInc.">CrimethInc.</a></div>
<p>CrimethInc. is a decentralized <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a> collective of autonomous <a href="/wiki/Clandestine_cell_system" title="Clandestine cell system">cells</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-99">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thompson_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-100">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ludwig_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ludwig-101">[97]</a></sup> CrimethInc. emerged in the mid-1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-faq-102">[98]</a></sup> initially as the hardcore  <a href="/wiki/Zine" title="Zine">zine</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inside_Front" title="Inside Front">Inside Front</a></i>, and began operating as a collective in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thompson_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-thompson-103">[99]</a></sup> It has since published widely read articles and zines for the anarchist movement and distributed posters and books of its own publication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brandt_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-brandt-104">[100]</a></sup> Individuals adopting the CrimethInc. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nom_de_guerre" title="Nom de guerre">nom de guerre</a></i>  have included convicted <a href="/wiki/Earth_Liberation_Front" title="Earth Liberation Front">ELF</a> <a href="/wiki/Arson" title="Arson">arsonists</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[101]</a></sup> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hacktivists" title="Hacktivists">hacktivists</a> who successfully attacked the websites of <a href="/wiki/Drug_Abuse_Resistance_Education" title="Drug Abuse Resistance Education">DARE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republican_National_Committee" title="Republican National Committee">Republican National Committee</a> and sites related to U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>'s <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush_presidential_campaign,_2004" title="George W. Bush presidential campaign, 2004">2004 re-election campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-wired-106">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deagon_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-deagon-107">[103]</a></sup> The creation of propaganda has been described as the collectives' core function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harper's_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-harper's-108">[104]</a></sup> Among their best-known publications are the books <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Days_of_War,_Nights_of_Love_(book)" title="Days of War, Nights of Love (book)">Days of War, Nights of Love</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expect_Resistance" title="Expect Resistance">Expect Resistance</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evasion_(book)" title="Evasion (book)">Evasion</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recipes_for_Disaster" title="Recipes for Disaster">Recipes for Disaster: An Anarchist Cookbook</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Pamphlet" title="Pamphlet">pamphlet</a> <i>Fighting For Our Lives</i> (of which, to date, they claim to have printed 600,000 copies),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[105]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk" title="Hardcore punk">hardcore punk</a>/political <a href="/wiki/Zine" title="Zine">zine</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inside_Front" title="Inside Front">Inside Front</a></i>, and the music of hardcore punk bands. As well as the traditional anarchist opposition to the <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, agents have, at times, advocated a <a href="/wiki/Straight_edge" title="Straight edge">straight edge</a> lifestyle, the total supersession of <a href="/wiki/Gender_role" title="Gender role">gender roles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gndr_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-gndr-110">[106]</a></sup> violent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurrection" title="Insurrection">insurrection</a> against the state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[107]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Refusal_of_work" title="Refusal of work">refusal of work</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vacation_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-vacation-112">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Direct_action">Direct action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Direct action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radical_environmental_movement" title="Radical environmental movement">Radical environmental movement</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_liberation_movement" title="Animal liberation movement">Animal liberation movement</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchism_and_animal_liberation" title="Anarchism and animal liberation">Anarchism and animal liberation</a></div>
<p>Some green anarchists engage in <a href="/wiki/Direct_action" title="Direct action">direct action</a> (not to be confused with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecoterrorism" title="Ecoterrorism">ecoterrorism</a>). Organizing themselves through groups like <a href="/wiki/Earth_First!" title="Earth First!">Earth First!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Root_Force" title="Root Force">Root Force</a>, or more drastically the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Liberation_Front" title="Earth Liberation Front">Earth Liberation Front</a> ELF, <a href="/wiki/Earth_Liberation_Army" title="Earth Liberation Army">Earth Liberation Army</a> (ELA) and <a href="/wiki/Animal_Liberation_Front" title="Animal Liberation Front">Animal Liberation Front</a> (ALF). They may take direct action against what they see as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systematic_oppression" title="Systematic oppression">systems of oppression</a>, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logging_industry" title="Logging industry">logging industry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Meat_industry" title="Meat industry">meat</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dairy_industry" title="Dairy industry">dairy industries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animal_testing" title="Animal testing">animal testing</a> laboratories, <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetic engineering facilities</a> and, more rarely, government institutions.
</p><p>Such actions are usually, though not always, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-violent" title="Non-violent">non-violent</a>, with groups such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Olga_Cell&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Olga Cell (page does not exist)">The Olga Cell</a> attempting assassinations of nuclear scientists, and other related groups sending letterbombs to nano tech and nuclear tech-related targets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature2012_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nature2012-113">[109]</a></sup> Though not necessarily Green anarchists, activists have used the names <a href="/wiki/Animal_Rights_Militia" title="Animal Rights Militia">Animal Rights Militia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justice_Department_(animal_rights_group)" title="Justice Department (animal rights group)">Justice Department</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Cells_-_Animal_Liberation_Brigade" title="Revolutionary Cells - Animal Liberation Brigade">Revolutionary Cells</a> among others, to claim responsibility for openly violent attacks.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Convictions">Convictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Convictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/GANDALF_trial" title="GANDALF trial">GANDALF trial</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SHAC_7" title="SHAC 7">SHAC 7</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stop_Huntingdon_Animal_Cruelty#Operation_Achilles" title="Stop Huntingdon Animal Cruelty">Stop Huntingdon Animal Cruelty § Operation Achilles</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rod_Coronado" title="Rod Coronado">Rod Coronado</a> is an eco-anarchist and is an unofficial spokesperson for the Animal Liberation Front and <a href="/wiki/Earth_Liberation_Front" title="Earth Liberation Front">Earth Liberation Front</a>. On February 28, 1992, Coronado carried out an <a href="/wiki/Arson" title="Arson">arson</a> attack on research facilities at <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">Michigan State University</a> (MSU), and released <a href="/wiki/Mink" title="Mink">mink</a> from a nearby research farm on campus, an action claimed by the ALF, and for which Coronado was subsequently convicted.
</p><p>In 1997, the editors of <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Anarchist" title="Green Anarchist">Green Anarchist</a></i> magazine and two British supporters of the Animal Liberation Front were tried in connection with conspiracy to incite violence, in what came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/GANDALF_trial" title="GANDALF trial">GANDALF trial</a>.
</p><p>Green anarchist <a href="/wiki/Tre_Arrow" title="Tre Arrow">Tre Arrow</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[111]</a></sup> was sought by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a> in connection with an ELF <a href="/wiki/Arson" title="Arson">arson</a> on April 15, 2001 at Ross Island Sand and Gravel in Portland, torching three trucks amounting of $200,000 in damage. Another arson occurred a month later at Ray Schoppert Logging Company in <a href="/wiki/Estacada,_Oregon" title="Estacada, Oregon">Estacada, Oregon</a>, on June 1, 2001 against logging trucks and a front loader, resulting in $50,000 damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oregon_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-oregon-116">[112]</a></sup> Arrow was indicted by a federal grand jury in Oregon and charged with four felonies for this crime on October 18, 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnvNews_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-EnvNews-117">[113]</a></sup> On March 13, 2004, after fleeing to <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, he was arrested in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria</a> for stealing bolt cutters and was also charged with being in Canada illegally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-rolling-118">[114]</a></sup> He was then sentenced on August 12, 2008 to 78 months in federal prison for his part in the arson and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" title="Conspiracy (crime)">conspiracy</a> ELF attacks in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2006, <a href="/wiki/Eric_McDavid" title="Eric McDavid">Eric McDavid</a>, a green anarchist,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[118]</a></sup> was convicted of conspiring to use fire or explosives to damage corporate and government property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hedlund_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-hedlund-123">[119]</a></sup> On March 8, he formally declared a <a href="/wiki/Hunger_strike" title="Hunger strike">hunger strike</a> due to the jail refusing to provide him with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vegan" title="Vegan">vegan</a> food. He has been given vegan food off and on since.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[120]</a></sup> In September 2007, he was convicted on all counts after the two activists he <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" title="Conspiracy (crime)">conspired</a> with pleaded guilty testified against him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hedlund_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-hedlund-123">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sacbee_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-sacbee-125">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[122]</a></sup> An FBI <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confidential_source" title="Confidential source">confidential source</a> named "Anna" was revealed as a fourth participant, in what McDavid's defense argued was <a href="/wiki/Entrapment" title="Entrapment">entrapment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_Sac:_freed_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_Sac:_freed-127">[123]</a></sup> In May 2008, he was sentenced to nearly 20 years in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 3, 2006, a federal jury in <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">Trenton, New Jersey</a> convicted six members of SHAC, including green-anarchist Joshua Harper,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-josh_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-josh-130">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecoterror_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecoterror-131">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[128]</a></sup> for "terrorism and Internet stalking", according to the <i>New York Times</i>, finding them guilty of using their website to "incite attacks" on those who did business with <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon_Life_Sciences" title="Huntingdon Life Sciences">Huntingdon Life Sciences</a> HLS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[129]</a></sup> In September 2006, the SHAC 7 received jail sentences of 3 to 6 years.
</p>
<dl><dt>Other prisoners</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Camenisch" title="Marco Camenisch">Marco Camenisch</a>: Swiss green anarchist accused of arson against electricity pylon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elpsn_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-elpsn-135">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>Nicole Vosper: green anarchist who pleaded guilty to charges against HLS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supportnic_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-supportnic-136">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nicole_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-nicole-137">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marius_Mason" title="Marius Mason">Marius Mason</a> (born Marie Jeanette Mason): serving 21 years and 10 months (#04672-061, FMC Carswell, Federal Medical Center, P.O. Box 27137, Fort Worth, TX 76127, USA) for his involvement in an ELF arson against a University building carrying out Genetically Modified crop tests. Marius also pleaded guilty to conspiring to carry out ELF actions and admitted involvement in 12 other ELF actions. (vegan).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marie_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-marie-138">[134]</a></sup></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Henri Zisly, self-labeled individualist anarchist, is considered one of the forerunners and principal organizers of the naturist movement in France and one of its most able and outspoken defenders worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boni_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boni-29">[29]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> censorship meant that many of Tolstoy's non-fiction works in the 1880s and 1890s were published abroad first, either in Russian or in translation, delaying the author's influence in his country of birth. However, with <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Chertkov" title="Vladimir Chertkov">Vladimir Chertkov</a> (1854–1936) as a key promoter of Tolstoy's ideas, a movement started over the 1890s. The movement continued to grow after the writer's death and was at its strongest in the years immediately following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_(1917)" title="Russian Revolution (1917)">revolutions of 1917</a> with agricultural communities established in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Smolensk_Oblast" title="Smolensk Oblast">Smolensk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tver_Oblast" title="Tver Oblast">Tver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samara_Oblast" title="Samara Oblast">Samara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kursk_Oblast" title="Kursk Oblast">Kursk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perm_Oblast" title="Perm Oblast">Perm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiev_Oblast" title="Kiev Oblast">Kiev</a>. The Tolstoyan communities that proliferated between 1917 and 1921 were eventually wiped out or stripped of their independence as <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Collectivization in the Soviet Union">collectivisation</a> and ideological purges got under way in the late 1920s. Colonies, such as the <a href="/wiki/Life_and_Labor_Commune" title="Life and Labor Commune">Life and Labor Commune</a>, relocated to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> to avoid being liquidated. Several Tolstoyan leaders, including <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yakov_Dragunovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yakov Dragunovsky (page does not exist)">Yakov Dragunovsky</a> (1886-1937), were put on trial and then sent to the <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Gulags</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChatfieldIli͡ukhina1994_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChatfieldIli͡ukhina1994-49">[48]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> John Coleman Kenworthy of the <a href="/wiki/Brotherhood_Church" title="Brotherhood Church">Brotherhood Church</a> established a colony at <a href="/wiki/Purleigh" title="Purleigh">Purleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a> in 1896. This community closed a few years later but its residents spawned the <a href="/wiki/Whiteway_Colony" title="Whiteway Colony">Whiteway Colony</a> in Gloucestershire and <a href="/wiki/Stapleton_Colony" title="Stapleton Colony">Stapleton Colony</a> in Yorkshire, both of which are still going today. Although given Whiteway soon abandoned Tolstoy's principles, it has been regarded by many, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohandas_Karamchand_Gandhi" title="Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi">Gandhi</a> who visited in 1909, as a failed Tolstoyan experiment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hunt2005_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt2005-51">[49]</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Johannes Van der Veer was the key figure in the Dutch Tolstoyan movement. In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> two colonies were started, a short-lived one at <a href="/wiki/Bussum" title="Bussum">Bussum</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a> and a more successful one nearby at <a href="/wiki/Blaricum" title="Blaricum">Blaricum</a>. The reasons attributed to the failure of Tolstoyan communities across Europe have included the personal incompatibility of the participants and a general lack of practical agricultural experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christoyannopoulos2013_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Christoyannopoulos2013-53">[50]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"While almost all forms of modern anarchism consider themselves to have an ecological dimension, the specifically eco-anarchist thread within anarchism has two main focal points, Social Ecology and "primitivist"."<a class="external autonumber" href="http://anarchism.pageabode.com/afaq/secA3.html#seca33" rel="nofollow">[1]</a><a href="/wiki/An_Anarchist_FAQ" title="An Anarchist FAQ">An Anarchist FAQ</a><span> by Various authors</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Thoreau-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Thoreau_9-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Thoreau_9-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">"Su obra más representativa es Walden, aparecida en 1854, aunque redactada entre 1845 y 1847, cuando Thoreau decide instalarse en el aislamiento de una cabaña en el bosque, y vivir en íntimo contacto con la naturaleza, en una vida de soledad y sobriedad. De esta experiencia, su filosofía trata de transmitirnos la idea que resulta necesario un retorno respetuoso a la naturaleza, y que la felicidad es sobre todo fruto de la riqueza interior y de la armonía de los individuos con el entorno natural. Muchos han visto en Thoreau a uno de los precursores del ecologismo y del anarquismo primitivista representado en la actualidad por <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a>. Para George Woodcock, esta actitud puede estar también motivada por una cierta idea de resistencia al progreso y de rechazo al materialismo creciente que caracteriza la sociedad norteamericana de mediados de siglo XIX."<a class="external text" href="http://www.acracia.org/xdiez.html" rel="nofollow">"LA INSUMISIÓN VOLUNTARIA. EL ANARQUISMO INDIVIDUALISTA ESPAÑOL DURANTE LA DICTADURA Y LA SEGUNDA REPÚBLICA (1923-1938)" by Xavier Diez</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060526224800/http://www.acracia.org/xdiez.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2006-05-26 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"De hecho, el documento de Isaac Puente se convirtió en dictamen oficial aprobado en el Congreso Extraordinario Confederal de Zaragoza de 1936 que servía de base para fijar la línea política de la CNT respecto a la organización social y política futura. La versión completa se puede encontrar en las actas oficiales del congreso, publicadas en CNT: El Congreso Confederal de Zaragoza, Zeta, Madrid, 1978, pp. 226-242." <li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Los anarco-individualistas, G.I.A...Una escisión de la FAI producida en el IX Congreso (Carrara, 1965) se pr odujo cuando un sector de anarquistas de tendencia humanista rechazan la interpretación que ellos juzgan disciplinaria del <i>pacto asociativo" clásico, y crean los GIA (Gruppi di Iniziativa Anarchica) . Esta pequeña federación de grupos, hoy nutrida sobre todo de veteranos anarco-individualistas de orientación pacifista, naturista, etcétera defiende la autonomía personal y rechaza a rajatabla toda forma de intervención en los procesos del sistema, como sería por ejemplo el sindicalismo. Su portavoz es L'Internazionale con sede en Ancona. La escisión de los GIA prefiguraba, en sentido contrario, el gran debate que pronto había de comenzar en el seno del movimiento"<a class="external text" href="http://eljorobado.enlucha.info/bicicleta/bicicleta/ciclo/01/17.htm" rel="nofollow">"El movimiento libertario en Italia" by </a></i><a class="external text" href="http://eljorobado.enlucha.info/bicicleta/bicicleta/ciclo/01/17.htm" rel="nofollow">Bicicleta. REVISTA DE COMUNICACIONES LIBERTARIAS<i> Year 1 No. Noviembre, 1 1977</i></a><i> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20131012054206/http://eljorobado.enlucha.info/bicicleta/bicicleta/ciclo/01/17.htm" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2013-10-12 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.</i></span>
